Education News Highlights

Japanese Secondary School Revolution 99

▲Sufficient for Reference by China's Education Sector

The Japanese secondary school system reform issue, which has been a topic of debate for many years, was announced by the Ministry of Education on January 10th of this year with the revision of the Secondary School Regulations, effective on April 10th. The main points are as follows:

1. The purpose of secondary schools is to build upon elementary school education, provide a higher level of moral education, national education, and useful general knowledge for life, and to promote physical education, in accordance with the spirit of the Secondary School Ordinance. Special attention should be paid to the following items: (1) Based on the Imperial Rescript on Education, moralize the entire school education and constantly guide students to practice and act. More attention should be paid to the cultivation of national morality, so that they can understand the essence of nation-building and the dignity of the national polity, the great righteousness of loyalty and filial piety, and consolidate their beliefs. (2) Strive to cultivate a spirit of independence and autonomy, a habit of loving labor, respect for cooperation, and appreciation for the virtue of responsibility. (3) Focus on inspiring mental power so that it is not restricted by the system of specialized academic disciplines, but rather cultivates knowledge and skills that are appropriate and useful for social life.

2. Secondary school graduation takes five years. The subjects are: Moral Education, Civics, Chinese Language and Literature, History, Geography, Foreign Language, Mathematics, Science, Industry, Drawing and Practical Work, and Physical Education. In the fourth year and above, two types of courses, First and Second, are created for students to choose from. The common basic subjects for both courses are Moral Education, Civics, Chinese Language and Literature, History, Geography, Science, and Physical Education. In addition to the basic subjects, the First Course may add Chinese Language and Literature, Foreign Language, Mathematics, Science, Drawing, Music, suitable teaching subjects, and Industry. In addition to the basic subjects, the Second Course may add suitable subjects from Chinese Language and Literature, Mathematics, Science, Drawing, and Music, and Foreign Language. The provisions of the preceding paragraph may also be applied from the third year, but the common basic subjects are Moral Education, Civics, Chinese Language, Literature, History, Geography, Mathematics, Science, Practical Work, and Physical Education. The First Course may add suitable teaching subjects from Chinese Language and Literature, Foreign Language, Mathematics, Science, Drawing, Music, and Industry. The First Course may add suitable subjects from Chinese Language, Teaching, Science, Drawing, and Music, and Foreign Language. In special circumstances, permission may be requested from the Ministry of Education to reduce the number of subjects. When Industry is taught in place of Industrial Arts or Agriculture, Practical Work may be omitted.

3. The number of teaching hours per week for each grade, when divided into First and Second Courses in the fourth year and above, uses the A Table. When divided into courses in the third year, uses the B Table. Music in the third year of Table A may be omitted. When Practical Work is omitted, the number of teaching hours may be allocated to other subjects. The teaching hours for practical work, drawing, music, etc., and physical education may be taught outside the time specified in Table A or Table 1. Outside of Table A or Table B, up to two hours per week may be used for extracurricular guidance. Table A and Table B are omitted.

4. The teaching of each subject should seek coordination to enhance its effectiveness.

5. The Industry subject teaches knowledge and skills related to industry, enabling students to understand practical life and cultivate a respect for occupation and a spirit of diligence.

The Industry subject is taught in agriculture, industry, or commerce, or a combination thereof, as appropriate.

6. The purpose of the Practical Work subject is to cultivate students' habit of loving labor and acquire useful knowledge and skills for daily life. The Practical Work subject is taught in gardening and other work. From the third year onwards, practical work focusing on instrumental drawing may be taught.

The above is a summary of the main points of the regulations. The focus of this revision is on the following points: (1) Attention to ideological guidance (2) Attention to separately designing courses A and B for students who can go on to higher education and students who cannot (3) Attention to vocational education (4) Attention to the languages of neighboring countries, namely Chinese (5) Adoption of mixed teaching methods (6) Attention to practical work education (7) Adding subjects outside of the basic subjects, which can be selected (8) Increasing the number of teaching hours for added subjects to provide flexibility.

Ministry of Education Investigates the Service of Returned Students 101

Yesterday, the Ministry of Education ordered the various cities to investigate the service of returned students. The order stated: "The original intention of our country in dispatching students to study abroad was to reserve specialized talents for construction, which is of great importance to the future of the country. Now that political tutelage has begun, there is a great need for talent. Whether returned students in the past have been able to meet the demand, and how the standards for future dispatch should be regulated, must first be carefully investigated in order to have a basis for decision-making. Two types of investigation forms have been prepared by the Ministry: (A) Investigation Form on the Current Service Status of Returned Students in the Country; (B) Investigation Form on Current Students Studying in Various Countries. The Ministry will simultaneously investigate students both at home and abroad for statistical purposes. In addition to sending them out separately, please find the enclosed copies of Form A and fill them out and return them. Please also forward them to your subordinates to fill out and send directly to the Ministry for statistical purposes. This is of public interest."

▲In the 20th Year, Shandong Province Will Add Rural Normal Schools and Secondary Schools

Jinan, 6th: The Director of the Department of Education, He Siyuan, approved that in the 20th year, five normal schools will be added in Pingyuan, six rural normal schools will be established in Huimin, and thirteen secondary schools will be added. The existing secondary and normal schools will increase enrollment by 30 classes. Qingdao University will be renamed Shandong University.

Our ministry now plans to compile and specially create a survey form for current employees, conducting separate surveys of agencies nationwide in order to compile and print it in the shortest possible time. In addition to directly sending it to the education departments of various provinces for verification, please also forward the aforementioned survey form and ask them to fill it out and send it back. Please also forward the notification to the various national universities under your jurisdiction and ask them to fill it out in accordance with the instructions in the form and send it to the ministry so that it can be compiled and printed. Furthermore, the deadline for this investigation by our ministry is July 31st of this year. Libraries to be Established in All Counties of Anhui Province 104

▲To be managed by the Party Committee...Circular from the Provincial Propaganda Department

The county Party committees of Anhui have repeatedly submitted proposals to the Provincial Reorganization Committee to allocate funds to establish libraries. The Provincial Reorganization Committee has found that the Provincial Executive Committee before January of the 19th year had set up regulations for counties to establish libraries and a budget for expenses, and the Provincial Government had discussed and decided to follow them, and circulated them to the counties. The method divides the counties into four levels: Huaining and other counties are in the first level, with an initial cost of 670 yuan and a monthly recurring cost of 40 yuan; Nanling and other counties are in the second level, with an initial cost of 600 yuan and a monthly recurring cost of 40 yuan; Susong and other counties are in the third level, with an initial cost of 530 yuan and a monthly recurring cost of 40 yuan; Langxi and other counties are in the fourth level, with the initial cost and recurring cost undefined. The funds are allocated from the educational expenses of each county and are managed by the county propaganda department. The Provincial Propaganda Department yesterday also ordered all counties to follow the original plan.

▲ Mandarin Speech Competition...April 15

▲ English Debate Preliminary...May 25

Guanghua, Fudan, Jiaotong, and Ji Nan Universities hold two Chinese and English speech and debate competitions each year. The preparatory meeting for this semester's Mandarin speech and English debate was held from 12:00 PM to 2:00 PM on March 1 at the Da Zhonghua Restaurant on Sichuan Road. Representatives from the four universities attended: Zhang Xinglian from Guanghua, Zhang Yi from Fudan, Li Songtao and Tang Qingyi from Jiaotong, and Rao Shu and Guo Shuliang from Ji Nan. The speech topics will be chosen by each participant and approved by the authorities of their respective schools. Prizes will be awarded for both team and individual performances. The judging criteria are "Material 30%", "Thought 30%", "Pronunciation 20%", and "Posture 20%". The topic is "Resolved, that we should pity our grandchildren." The preliminary round pairings were determined by drawing lots: Guanghua and Fudan as one group, with Guanghua arguing for the affirmative and Fudan for the negative, to be held at Guanghua; Jiaotong and Ji Nan as one group, with Jiaotong arguing for the affirmative and Ji Nan for the negative, to be held at Jiaotong. The affirmative/negative positions and location of the final round will be determined by the two universities that win the preliminary rounds. Each school will send three representatives, limited to university students, one as the main debater and two as assistant debaters. The Business School of National Central University has completed the construction of its new campus at 1000 West Jiangwan Sports Association Road. The structure is new and the equipment is perfect. The female dormitories are located on the fourth floor of the main building and are very well-equipped. All documents coming to and from the school can be sent directly to Jiangwan. The No. 1 public bus from Zhabei North goes directly to the school gate, making transportation very convenient. The opening ceremony and celebration of the completion of the new campus will be held on April 1.

Recording a Guest's Talk About Wu Changshuo's Portrait 125

— Zheng Yimei

Among paintings, there is what is called "conveying the spirit," which means using brush and ink to depict a person's appearance and capturing their spirit. The two words "conveying the spirit" first appeared in "A New Account of Tales of the World." Gu Changkang painted people, sometimes not dotting the eyes for several years. When people asked him why, he said that conveying the spirit lies precisely in the "a du." Common depictions of the spirit mostly are rigid and dull, creating an image of someone sitting upright in formal attire, with a craftsman's touch filling the paper, so rotten it makes one want to vomit. Famous painters are ashamed to do so. However, taking pictures for virtuous people, arranging garden scenery, and not adding detailed descriptions of clothing, resulting in an elegant style, can also create world-renowned works. Ren Yi (Bonian), from Shanyin, painted Wu Changshuo's portrait among banana trees on a stone bed. Changshuo exposed his body, waving a cattail fan, sitting on it. A sense of leisure is abundantly revealed in the silk painting. It is truly a masterpiece by Ren. After Changshuo's death, his collection of paintings was printed as a collotype at the end. Last year, the Wu Changshuo Painting Exhibition was opened at the 63rd Garden on Jiangwan Road. I have always admired Old Cang and, since the 63rd Garden is close to my residence, I went to visit once. Ren Bonian's portrait was hung high on the white wall. The brush strokes are ancient and elegant, completely different from ordinary depictions of the spirit. Facing it makes one imagine the predecessors' elegance without end. The painting is deeply imprinted in my mind, and it has been a year or two since then. A guest who is familiar with Changshuo's life said that Ren's portrait was not initially a portrait of Changshuo. The portrait has a short stature and is robust, which matches Changshuo perfectly. Changshuo got it, carved out its head and face, asked someone to draw his own face, and then had it mounted. It was patched up perfectly, like a seamless garment. As the saying goes, "changing the head and face," Changshuo actually carried it out mischievously. Whether the guest's account is accurate or not is unknown, but the matter is quite interesting, so it is recorded. It serves as an interpretation for those who care about the art world.

A Test of Standards for Choosing a Husband for Female Students in Dalian 126

— Green Pearl

Dalian Japanese newspaper reports that. The top girls' school in Dalian is the Yayoi Higher Girls' School. The school has always paid attention to issues such as the future of graduates. The recent implementation of the test of standards for choosing a husband has been even more sensational. This year's spring graduates. A total of one hundred and eighty-seven. The principal, in order to understand their hopes for future marriage. Printed a kind of form. Divide the columns such as qualifications and occupations. Issued to each graduate to fill in. In order to understand the attitudes of each graduate towards choosing a husband. Result. It is willing that the husband be a company employee. Occupies one hundred and ten votes. Ten votes for general salary earners. Eighteen votes for teachers. Twenty-five votes for entrepreneurs. Only thirteen votes for officials. There are eight votes for other wives who want their husbands to be soldiers. Among them, six votes. Those who wish their husbands to engage in the army have two votes. The rest hope to engage in the navy. Four votes for those who hope to choose a politician as a husband. There are only two votes for those who hope to choose an artist as a husband. Nine votes for those who idealize a doctor as a husband. As for those who hope that their future husband will engage in agriculture and freelance occupations. Only one vote each. In summary, among these one hundred and eighty-seven votes, the educational level of the husband is specified. It is estimated that about 50% of the graduates hope to graduate from secondary schools or above. No more than twenty-two people specified that they must graduate from university. The most interesting thing is. That is, among these one hundred and eighty-seven votes. It is specified that those who absolutely oppose drinking alcohol. There are more than one hundred and fifty votes. As for the smoking issue. Almost all of them take a lenient attitude. According to the school principal's disclosure. It is said that among the one hundred and ten votes for those who want their husbands to be company employees. Most of them specify that they are most satisfied with employees engaged in the South Manchurian Railway. This is because those who engage in the South Manchurian Railway. Most can get generous salaries.

Early Spring Snack Recipes 127

— Yang Yixiao

▲ Steamed Small Yellow Croaker with Shrimp Oil Take a small yellow croaker. After washing, add two spoons of shrimp oil. A pinch of clear salt. Place on the rice pot and steam until cooked. Fresh and delicious.

▲ Chives Sprout Mixed with Crab Paste Skin Use hairy crabs and duck eggs. Spread a sheet of crab paste skin. Cut into narrow, long, thin slices. Mix with chives sprouts. Add a little soy sauce vinegar again. Absolutely delicious.

▲ Snail Meat Stir-fried with Shrimp Kernels After shelling the periwinkles and fresh shrimps. Put them in a hot wok with lard. Add a little good soy sauce. Stir-fry two or three times and then stop. Fresh and tender.

▲ Bamboo Shoot Stored with Fresh Meat Paste Remove the shell from the bamboo shoot. Cut it open and take fresh meat and chop it into a paste. Store it in the basket. Put it in a wok. Add soy sauce and braise it. Add agaric after it is cooked. The taste is unusually rich and beautiful.

An Essay on Ancient Egyptian Beetle Amulets 128

— Zou Jinshi

On New Year's Day, I, along with Mr. and Mrs. Ge Mei and Mr. and Mrs. Liu Fan You, visited the bookplate exhibition at the Mingfu Library. Among them, there were no fewer than hundreds of meticulously printed and copied books from the Song, Yuan, Ming, and Qing dynasties, classified and displayed, gathering secret copies from collectors all over the country in one hall for public viewing. This is not only a joyful event for the moment but also an unprecedented grand occasion in thousands of years. It is truly delightful. Besides these, the oracle bones from the Yin Ruins, the clay seals from Qi and Lu, the bronze seals from the Qin and Han dynasties, the handwritten scriptures from the Tang dynasty, and the scriptures hidden in the Leifeng Pagoda are all rare treasures in the world, exuding an ancient and fragrant atmosphere that fills the room. What is particularly peculiar is the ancient Egyptian beetle amulets collected by Mr. Zhang Tianfang, which are truly something I have never seen or heard of before. The amulets are all oval in shape, the large ones are like thumbs, and the small ones are only like melon seeds. The back is carved with the image of a beetle, hence the name. The abdomen is engraved with characters, with a small hole in the middle, presumably for threading a rope to wear as a pendant. The body color is emerald green, and at first glance, it looks exactly like a beetle. As a person with an addiction to antiquities, I was immediately amazed and overjoyed. I exclaimed, "Is the use of amulets and seals unique to our country?" Unfortunately, Mr. Zhang was not present, so I could not question him face to face. More than a month later, I visited my old friend Mr. Cao Liwu at Jinan University and, through Liwu's introduction, I met Mr. Tianfang. I immediately asked to see the ancient seals. At that time, Mr. Zhang was resting at home due to illness, but he readily got up and showed me the seals, teaching me earnestly. There were a total of forty-five seals (two of which had no characters). The material was either stone or pottery, with ancient mottled colors, probably objects from thousands of years ago, which he obtained while studying in France. Each one was worth about four or five yuan at the time. Not only have they never been seen in China before, but even foreign collectors rarely see them. They are extremely precious and secretive. Examining the characters, they are mostly auspicious words or words related to deities, presumably worn on the chest to ward off misfortune. The script is ancient, peculiar, and exquisite, with its own unique style. Some seals have several characters, while others have only one character. The composition is balanced and harmonious, delicate and meticulous. Some have images of the sun, moon, mountains, and rivers; some are like nude women dancing or sitting in meditation playing the qin; some are like holding reins and standing, or carrying a staff and walking. The origin of Egyptian writing can be seen in these. I caressed them for a long time, reluctant to let go. I then made rubbings by hand. Because the seals were too small, it was difficult to pick them up. It took half a day to complete forty-three rubbings, and my fingers were already unbearably sore. After finishing the rubbings, I rested for a while. Mr. Zhang then showed me dozens of ancient Egyptian porcelain and stone artifacts, all of which were exquisite and delightful. Mr. Zhang is proficient in poetry and prose and also deeply versed in archaeology, so his collections are numerous and exquisite. He presented me with his volume of archaeological studies and the "Nancun Collection." I then bid farewell and left, returning home to record the entire process with my pen, to inform gentlemen who love antiquities at home and abroad.

Supplementary Notes on Pinching Likenesses 129

— Qing Qu

After my previous article "Recording Likenesses Pinched by Hand" was published, I received information from friends stating that the former generation of Mr. Gu Zhiwei and Mr. Gu Jianzhou of Jiayi also had portraits left behind, which were sculpted at the time and remain intact to this day. It is a great pity that I have not been able to see them.

Just yesterday, Mr. Ge Jiantan also said that there are still masters of likeness pinching today. A friend of his in Shanghai had a portrait of a couple pinched, sometime in the spring of the year before last. The sculptor was hired from Guangfu Township in Suzhou, but his name is now lost. However, he remembers that his surname was Zheng, and it is not easy to obtain his permission. One must go through intermediaries to urge him to come and try his skills. When he arrives, one cannot treat him merely as an artisan but must be sincere and respectful, as if treating a distinguished guest. His work involves sitting face to face with the person, always doing it under the table. Therefore, the person never knows how he does it. It takes more than a month for the portrait to be completed. The face is not allowed to be shown until it is finished, and even if the folds of the clothes are complete, the shoes and birds are not finished, it is still kept secret. When it is seen, it is lifelike and vibrant. Whether one knows the person or not, one can recognize them and point out their name. Such is the magic of his skill. He also said that the cost is very high. Each portrait costs nearly a hundred yuan, not including the cost of food, drinks, and rest.

According to the above description, it is similar to the facts I previously recorded, but the timing is different. It is probably another person, but with the same skills. The only similarity is that they are both from Suzhou. Although their names are unknown, I believe someone must know them. Perhaps they are direct descendants of the same school, so they can shine successively in the world. I have a strong interest in the arts, especially the masterpieces. I cannot help but describe them again and again. I also hope that those who are knowledgeable can expand on this.

A Record of Reviving Fish by Boiling 130

— Wu Jiren

Last winter was severely cold, unprecedented in Nanzhong for thirty years. My wife, Fu Ji, and I happened to be traveling in the countryside. We had no companions on the journey and only brought thirty of our favorite fine goldfish with us. However, the countryside was bitterly cold, and with frequent rain and snow, the climate was colder than in the city. Although we placed them indoors and changed the well water once a day to keep their body temperature from freezing, eight goldfish with upturned gills and celestial eyes simultaneously had difficulty swimming on their sides. Their breathing was also very rapid. Shortly after, their breathing slowed down, and their spirits gradually stopped. Four fish actually floated to the surface and died. I was quite reluctant, but since there was no fragrance of resurrection, I let it be. Suddenly, Fu Ji said to me, "Treat a dead horse as if it were a live one. Why not move them into warm water and see if they can revive?" I tried it as she said. In a short while, they actually showed signs of life. I was very happy. I poured more water into the pot, and the fish were moved in. When the charcoal was hot and the water gradually heated up, the fish also gradually moved. Their breathing in the gills also became more frequent. Soon, they were swimming as if they were alive, without any sluggishness. When I tested the water with my finger, it was about to boil. I quickly changed the well water. To this day, they are still safe and sound. Fu Ji laughed and said, "You have invented this method of reviving fish by boiling. Why don't you write it and send it to Mr. Juan?" I smiled and responded, writing this to inform fish lovers.

Mr. Hu Tianbai, I have received your letter. "Hongwei's Sentimental Recollections" is a short piece in parallel prose and was published in the "Nanshe Congkan" (now lost and unavailable). There is no separate book. Respectfully, your brother, Juan.

Correction: In yesterday's "A Word of Insight," the name signed "Cai Shangsi" should be "Cai Ensi." Also, the author of "Monkeys Addicted to Tobacco" is "Jianfu," mistakenly written as "Cangfu." We hereby correct these.

Random Talks on European Travel (2) 131

— Wang Yachen

About an hour after leaving the Rome station, we arrived at the Italian coast. Looking out at the horizon from the train window, I saw only a strip of white light appearing through the mist. The weather in Italy in April is the best time of the year. The sky is slightly cloudy. A few white gulls were foraging on the sea. The coolness of the morning was refreshing. This gentle feeling of late spring made the travelers feel happy. Along the way, we passed countless straits. The artificial decorations all contained a sense of beauty. Although not as excellent as Switzerland, it was enough for us to admire. At two o'clock in the afternoon, the train stopped at Pisa in central Italy. This place has a leaning tower, a place where poets and painters linger and are reluctant to leave. Especially in the history of art, it is extremely famous.

In central Italy, the Cathedoral church that we can see now was built between 1063 and 1092. It mainly adopts the basilica style, with some byyantium elements added. Its gorgeous and majestic characteristics can be called the initial form of romanesque architecture. Later, churches modeled after this style could be seen throughout Europe.

Visiting the Cathedoral church in Pisa is enough to satisfy us, but there are also two world-famous buildings: the Leaning Tower and the Baptistery. The Leaning Tower campanite is named for its leaning shape. One theory is that the ground subsided during construction, causing it to lean. Another theory is that the tower was deliberately tilted when it was built. This is a building from 1117. The whole body is seven stories with arched openings, with a round tower on top. The inclination is thirty-three feet. The colors are ancient and mottled. Its grandeur is unparalleled. The magnificence of the Baptistery, although not as great as the Leaning Tower, is more beautiful than the Leaning Tower and the Cathedoral church. It was built in 1153. The plan is circular, with a diameter of one hundred and twenty-nine feet. It is made entirely of marble. Looking at the whole, it has a simple characteristic.

After visiting Pisa for four hours, we took the train again. A French clergyman came into the same carriage. He was serving in the Vatican. He was very amiable. The clergyman told us the story of the Leaning Tower, which, although containing religious significance, has a close relationship with art. European countries maintain historical antiquities very completely. Although the tower has been leaning for more than eight hundred years, it has not collapsed because people often take care of it and have repeatedly repaired it, preserving its ancient meaning.

The Yarn and Cotton Market Experiences a Sharp Decline 137

The yarn market suddenly weakened, and the decline was severe. The rapid changes in recent days have left people bewildered. The market fluctuates greatly, rising and falling unpredictably. This situation is entirely affected by the financial wave. In addition, rumors are rife in the business community, and people are panicked. The spot yarn market is lifeless, and the marked yarn at 177-178 taels is already a high level and is prone to changes in response to any news. In fact, there is an upward trend, but the actual demand is sluggish because domestic farmers' purchasing power is insufficient. The higher the price, the more stagnant the transaction. The future of the yarn market is difficult to predict.

The Garrison Headquarters Prepares to Commemorate the Fallen Soldiers 152

▲ Time: 8:00 AM on the 10th

▲ Location: Public Stadium

The Songhu Garrison Headquarters received a telegram from the Preparatory Office of the Nanjing Memorial Service for the Fallen Soldiers, urgently forwarding it to various public groups for their information. The General Headquarters of the Army, Navy, and Air Force initiated a memorial service for the fallen soldiers who died fighting against the rebels, which is scheduled to be held at the Capital Public Stadium for three days starting from March 10. Now, nine unified measures for the whole country have been formulated: (1) The memorial tablet for the fallen soldiers shall be 3 feet 5 inches high and read: "The tablet of the Army, Navy, and Air Force soldiers who died fighting against the rebels." (2) All localities in the country, except the capital, shall hold a memorial service at 8:00 AM on March 10, with Party, government, and military organs, schools, mass vocational groups, etc., gathering at a wide location in their respective locations, following the central government's memorial ceremony and formulating their own etiquette. All participants shall wear black纱 on their arms. (3) All units of the Army, Navy, and Air Force throughout the country, whether or not they have representatives participating in Beijing, shall gather at 8:00 AM on the same morning at their respective locations to hold a memorial service, or may also hold it together with the organs, groups, etc. (4) The Army, Navy, and Air Force throughout the country shall fire 33 salutes on the morning of that day. (5) Aircraft in various localities shall fly and distribute propaganda materials or blue paper scraps. (6) All factories throughout the country shall fire 33 salutes on the morning of that day. (7) All parts of the country shall fly the flag at half-mast for three days starting from March 10. (8) All banquets throughout the country shall be suspended for one day on this day. (9) All newspapers throughout the country shall publish the twelve characters "Memorial to the Army, Navy, and Air Force Soldiers Who Died Fighting Against the Rebels" on the first line of the cover on this day, bordered in black for one day. The above articles have been submitted to the Commander-in-Chief, forwarded to the National Government, and ordered to be followed, and forwarded to the Central Party Department. We hereby send the telegram again, hoping that you will check and deal with it and instruct your subordinates to do the same. As for the elegies, eulogies,联对 and poems, etc. of the martyrs of the fallen soldiers, please send them to our office as soon as possible for collection. After receiving the telegram, the Command Headquarters decided to hold the event at the China Public Stadium on the morning of March 10 and immediately notified all Party, government, and military organs in the city to attend the memorial service at that time to express their condolences. The order and ceremony of the大会 are as follows: (1) Date: March 10, morning. (2) Arrangement: The fence card shall be handled by the Adjutant Office of the Garrison Headquarters. (3) Ceremony: (A) Fire 33 salutes. (B) All stand in silence and bow three times to the portrait of the fallen soldiers. (C) Read the will.

(D) Silent for three minutes. (E) Offer flowers. (F) Read the memorial article. (G) The highest officer delivers a speech. (H) Representatives of various organs deliver speeches. (I) Speeches. (J) The whole body calls slogans. (K) Play mourning music. (L) The ceremony is over. The meeting will be closed on March 12, but no salutes will be fired and no memorial article will be read. (4) Slogans and slogans shall be drafted by the Municipal Party Department. (5) The Chairman of the Municipal Government, the Party Department, and the Chief of Staff shall accompany the sacrifice. (6) The black紗 shall be prepared by the adjutant. (7) The artillery shall fire 33 rounds. (8) The挽联 shall be sent to the Adjutant Office of the Command Headquarters for hanging at 12:00 on the 9th. (9) County government aspects, each group shall be notified by the county government. (10) The mayor and commander shall jointly announce to the public. (11) 26 regiments of the team shall be sent. (12) The Adjutant Office shall notify the military band Command Headquarters, the Public Security Bureau, and the newspaper cover. (13) The Command Headquarters shall notify the Navy Department and the Aviation Administration. (14) The reception shall be organized by the Command Headquarters, the Municipal Government, and the Municipal Party Department, each sending five or six people, and the reception staff shall be handled by the Adjutant Office of the Command Headquarters.

British Newspaper Predicts That Demand for Silver Will Increase 154

▲ The situation will improve after the Indian political problem is resolved.

According to the North China Daily News, the resolution of the Indian political problem is unlikely to have a good impact on the exchange rate in a day or two, but yesterday (5th), the popularity showed a good sign and the market was quite firm, probably because the demand for silver is about to increase and the exchange rate may increase. Not only can India's commerce fully reach this point, but also China's commerce. For example, from January to May of last year, the silk that China transported to India was worth one million taels of silver per month. Later, India implemented a boycott of foreign goods, and the silk transport stopped. Now it is expected that the commerce between the two countries will resume in a few days. This is a great benefit to China's export trade and is sufficient to benefit the exchange market. In addition, the trade between India and 英甸, especially for Lancashire, will have a turnaround due to the end of the boycott of foreign goods, and an effect of the same importance, or even more importance, is that India's silent export trade in recent months will be revived, so India must need more silver to be sent to the interior to pay for this item, which is also enough to make the market improve.

Japanese Scheme to Monopolize Northeast Shipping 155

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company plans to restore its Northeast shipping rights. The British Swire Company has also opened routes from Shantou and Xiamen to Guangdong. Japanese shipping companies, upon hearing this, have planned various countermeasures, fearing intense competition. The following is a special report:

▲China Merchants Designates Regular Liners. Li Zhonggong, Director-General of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, in order to develop Northeast shipping and recover lost shipping rights in Andong, Yingkou, etc., plans to add formal scheduled ships in the Northeast to transport goods such as soybeans from outside the customs. He ordered Shen Zhongyi, head of the business department, to conduct a detailed investigation and prepare for navigation. At the same time, Zhang Xiangcai was also commissioned to conduct on-the-spot inspections in Yingkou. As a result, it was decided to start shipping. Zhang Jicai has already submitted a report to Shanghai, listing detailed methods. After approval by Director-General Li, a branch office will be established in Yingkou, with Zhang as the branch manager. Now that the weather is gradually warming up, Yingkou will soon thaw. It has been decided to assign the company's largest ships, the "Gongping" and "Tunan," to serve as dedicated Shanghai-Yingkou liners, starting with the Shanghai-Yingkou route. After the company acquires new oceangoing vessels, it will add routes from Yingkou to Shantou, Xiamen, and Guangdong. The regulations for the branch office are being drafted, and the Yingkou port wharf is being repaired. Navigation will begin in one or two weeks.

▲Weihaiwei Line to Open Simultaneously. The Weihaiwei Port Administration requested that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company add Shanghai-Weihaiwei ships to boost the local economy, facilitate transportation, and develop commerce. Li Zhonggong accepted the request and dispatched the Zhifu branch manager to Weihai to set up an agency. It was originally planned to have Tianjin liners also serve the route, but since the "Xinming" is under repair and the "Xinfeng" has been transferred to the Yangtze River, it was decided to have the two newly opened Yingkou liners also serve this port and Dalian. Because of the urgency to start the service, a telegram was sent to Xu Zushen of the Weihaiwei Port Administration yesterday, urging the payment of 4,000 yuan as preparation funds for the new route. In the future, mail to Weihai will also be exclusively loaded by China Merchants ships.

▲Swire Company Dedicates Four Ships. The British Swire Company,

which previously did not have scheduled ships in Yingkou, has recently opened a dedicated route from Shantou and Xiamen to Guangdong to compete for the transport of miscellaneous grains from the Northeast. It has designated four oceangoing vessels, "Ganzhou," "Liangzhou," "Luzhou," and "De'an," to operate scheduled services, competing to load soybeans, sorghum, soybean cakes, millet, etc., to various ports in South China. Since the start of the service, business has been very successful, arousing the jealousy of Japanese merchants.

▲South Manchuria Railway Hastens to Compete for the Transport of Northeast Miscellaneous Grains. The transport of miscellaneous grains from the Northeast has always been dominated by Japan, and the South Manchuria Railway (Mantetsu) regards this as a vested right. Last year, it added 10 million yen of new capital to its affiliated Dalian Steamship Company to build eight new ships, four of which have already been completed. Its aim is to completely monopolize the export of goods from the three ports of Yingkou, Andong, and Dalian, using Mantetsu's land transportation to control all exports from the Northeast, preventing other countries' ships from getting involved. Last winter, it began a decisive battle to compete for transport with British Swire ships and Chinese Zhaoxing ships, recklessly cutting freight rates and disrupting cargo transport. Zhengji and other ships were severely affected, leading to staff reductions and salary cuts due to business losses. Swire entrusted a Japanese person to persuade Mantetsu to join a trade association and compete fairly by avoiding excessive rate cuts, but this was rejected by Mantetsu.

▲Intense Competition Imminent. Last year, Mantetsu made a profit of approximately 600,000 yuan. Once the second batch of four new ships is launched, it will open regular routes from Yingkou to South China. Recently, upon hearing that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is developing Northeast shipping routes, the Dalian Steamship Company considers it a formidable business rival. Therefore, at the recent shareholders' meeting, it proposed countermeasures against China Merchants' addition of Shanghai-Yingkou services. It is reported that it has been decided to use all of last year's profits to defend against Chinese ships. Once China Merchants ships start operating, freight rates will be drastically reduced, willing to use this huge amount of money to block Chinese ships from Northeast shipping. Therefore, the day China Merchants ships start operating the Shanghai-Yingkou route will mark the beginning of intense business competition among British, Japanese, and Chinese shipping companies, and a major upheaval is imminent, with the Japanese already preparing for it.

Organizational Rules and Operating Rules for the Municipal Election Office for National Assembly Representatives 160

Since yesterday, the Shanghai Municipal Election Office has been issuing registration forms to various organizations, causing its staff to become extremely busy. It is reported that the office held two meetings on the 2nd of this month and yesterday afternoon, passing the Organizational Rules and Operating Rules of the office, which have now been announced. Details are as follows:

Organizational Rules: Organizational Rules of the Shanghai Municipal Election Office for National Assembly Representatives. Article 1: In order to handle the election affairs of National Assembly Representatives, the Shanghai Municipal Election Office for National Assembly Representatives is established, subject to the guidance and supervision of the General Election Office for National Assembly Representatives. Article 2: The following matters shall be reported by this office to the General Election Office for National Assembly Representatives: (1) The organization and history of each organization with electoral qualifications; (2) The names and resumes of the election supervisors, ballot counting administrators, and voting administrators of each organization; (3) Matters regarding the investigation and punishment of electoral malpractices as stipulated in Article 17 of the National Assembly Representative Election Law; (4) Matters regarding the review and determination of re-elections as stipulated in Article 21 of the National Assembly Representative Election Law. Article 3: This office shall establish the following three sections to manage the affairs of each section: (1) General Affairs Section, responsible for documents, accounting, general affairs, and matters not belonging to other sections; (2) Review Section, responsible for reviewing the qualifications of various organizations, voters, and elected candidates; (3) Guidance Section, responsible for guiding election procedures. Article 4: The General Affairs Section shall be divided into the First, Second, and Third Subsections. Article 5: The functions of the First Subsection are as follows: (1) Matters regarding the seal and its safekeeping;

(2) Matters regarding the receipt and dispatch of documents; (3) Matters regarding the drafting of documents; (4) Matters regarding the copying of documents; (5) Matters regarding the official dispatch of documents; (6) Matters regarding the custody of archives; (7) Matters regarding the compilation of agendas for office meetings and the safekeeping of records; (8) Matters regarding the compilation of various registers and reports. Article 6: The functions of the Second Subsection are as follows: (1) Matters regarding the receipt and disbursement of funds; (2) Matters regarding the registration and safekeeping of books and vouchers. Article 7: The functions of the Third Subsection are as follows: (1) Matters regarding the purchase, registration, and safekeeping of goods; (2) Matters regarding election equipment; (3) Matters regarding the handling and safekeeping of printed materials; (4) Matters not belonging to other subsections. Article 8: The Review Section shall be divided into the First, Second, Third, Fourth, and Fifth Subsections. Article 9: The functions of the First Subsection are as follows: (1) Matters regarding the review of the qualifications of farmers' associations; (2) Matters regarding the review of the qualifications of voters and elected candidates of farmers' associations. Article 10: The functions of the Second Subsection are as follows: (1) Matters regarding the review of the qualifications of labor unions; (2) Matters regarding the review of the qualifications of voters and elected candidates of labor unions. Article 11: The functions of the Third Subsection are as follows: (1) Matters regarding the review of the qualifications of chambers of commerce and industrial organizations; (2) Matters regarding the review of the qualifications of voters and elected candidates of chambers of commerce and industrial organizations. Article 12: The functions of the Fourth Subsection are as follows: (1) Matters regarding the review of the qualifications of educational associations, national universities, and universities registered with the Ministry of Education; (2) Matters regarding the review of the qualifications of voters and elected candidates of educational associations, national universities, and universities registered with the Ministry of Education. Article 13: The functions of the Fifth Subsection are as follows: (1) Matters regarding the review of the qualifications of professional associations; (2) Matters regarding the review of the qualifications of voters and elected candidates of professional associations. Article 14: The Guidance Section shall be divided into the First, Second, Third, Fourth, and Fifth Subsections. Article 15: The functions of the First Subsection are as follows: (1) Matters regarding the guidance of election procedures for representatives of farmers' associations; (2) Matters regarding the registration of elections for representatives of farmers' associations. Article 16: The functions of the Second Subsection are as follows: (1) Matters regarding the guidance of election procedures for representatives of labor unions; (2) Matters regarding the registration of elections for representatives of labor unions. Article 17: The functions of the Third Subsection are as follows: (1) Matters regarding the guidance of election procedures for representatives of chambers of commerce and industrial organizations; (2) Matters regarding the registration of elections for representatives of chambers of commerce and industrial organizations. Article 18: The functions of the Fourth Subsection are as follows: (1) Matters regarding the guidance of election procedures for representatives of educational associations, national universities, and universities registered with the Ministry of Education; (2) Matters regarding the registration of elections for representatives of educational associations, national universities, and universities registered with the Ministry of Education. Article 19: The functions of the Fifth Subsection are as follows: (1) Matters regarding the guidance of election procedures for representatives of professional associations; (2) Matters regarding the registration of elections for representatives of professional associations. Article 20: The election supervisor of this office shall comprehensively manage affairs and direct and supervise the staff of this office and the personnel of various organizations handling election affairs. Article 21: This office shall establish a chief secretary and five secretaries, who shall handle affairs under the orders of the election supervisor. Article 22: Each section of this office shall have a section chief, concurrently held by a secretary; each subsection shall have a subsection chief, clerks, and secretaries, who shall handle affairs under the orders of their superiors. Article 23: The personnel in the preceding two articles shall be transferred from the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Government. Their duties shall be assigned by the election supervisor. Article 24: The office meeting of this office shall be organized by the election supervisor, the chief secretary, and the secretaries. Article 25: This office shall be abolished after the election is completed. Article 2

Page 14

6: The operating rules of this office shall be determined separately. Article 27: These rules shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Operating Rules: Operating Rules of the Shanghai Municipal Election Office for National Assembly Representatives. Article 1: These rules are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 26 of the organizational rules of this office. Article 2: The office meeting shall be organized in accordance with the organizational rules of this office; however, other staff members may also be designated by the election supervisor to attend and participate in discussions when necessary. Article 3: The election supervisor shall be the chairman of the office meeting. If the election supervisor is absent due to business, he may entrust the chief secretary to act as chairman on his behalf. Article 4: Matters for discussion shall include motions submitted by the election supervisor and proposals made by the chief secretary and secretaries. Other staff members may also make suggestions, but must obtain the permission of the election supervisor. Article 5: Resolved matters shall be submitted by the election supervisor to the relevant responsible section for handling. Article 6: The office meeting shall be held once a week; if necessary, the election supervisor may convene temporary meetings. Article 7: All incoming documents shall be abstracted and numbered daily by the receiving and dispatching clerk, submitted by the head of the General Affairs Section, and forwarded to the chief secretary for transmission to the election supervisor for review before being distributed to the various sections for separate handling. Article 8: All outgoing documents shall be properly drafted by the responsible personnel, submitted to the head of the section for review, forwarded to the chief secretary for transmission to the election supervisor for approval, and then submitted to the General Affairs Section for printing and distribution. Article 9: All completed documents shall be properly filed immediately. Article 10: Staff members of this office shall not publish documents to the outside world in the name of this office or the section. Article 11: Staff members of this office shall not copy or show documents of this office to others, or take documents of this office outside. The office hours of this office are from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 1:00 PM to 5:00 PM daily, except for Sundays and holidays. They may be advanced or extended when necessary. Article 13: This office shall designate a rotating duty officer on holidays and outside daily office hours to handle temporary incidents. Article 14: These rules may be amended at any time if there are any unaddressed matters. Article 15: These rules shall take effect from the date of approval by the election supervisor.

▲Issuance of First Flight Commemorative Envelopes

After the establishment of the Sino-German joint venture Eurasia Aviation Corporation, it is actively proceeding. The organization by the Ministry has been completed. The company is located on the third floor of the Zhongfu Bank on Renji Road. Aircraft have been successively transported and will begin flying soon. It is reported that the company will issue the first Eurasia Flight Commemorative Envelope during the week of the first flight, and the post office will specially stamp a commemorative postmark on the airmail stamps. All letters sent to Beijing, Ping, Manzhouli, and European countries can be purchased for commemoration.

According to the Da Mei Evening News, the aircraft of the Eurasia Airlines were originally scheduled to be assembled and test-flown by the end of this week. However, due to cloudy and rainy weather, coupled with delays in the installation project, they could not depart as scheduled. According to Schmidt, if the weather clears up in the future, the first test flight should be able to depart from Shanghai next Wednesday or Thursday. After the two aircraft used were transported last week, it was originally planned to assemble them all at the Hongqiao Airport. However, due to the excessive weight of the fuselage of one aircraft, there were no vehicles available for transport, so the aircraft parts had to be transported back to the warehouse for assembly. It was not until yesterday that the assembly was completed, and this morning (the 6th), the tail was supported by a car and pushed to the airport. The wings were transported by other vehicles and will also be assembled today. It is estimated that short-range test flights will be conducted near this city next Monday or Tuesday. The company has two more aircraft, which will be shipped by the Hengmei Company's Cooperland liner and will arrive in Shanghai on the 9th of this month.

Flight between Shanghai and Yichang 162

▲Realization Set for the 16th

The China National Aviation Corporation is preparing to extend the Shanghai-Hankou route to Yichang. The company has scheduled to implement the flight on the 16th of this month, dispatching a recently refurbished Stinson aircraft to Hankou for use. It is scheduled to fly three times a week on Mondays, Wednesdays, and Fridays. It will take off from Hankou at 8:15 AM, arrive in Yichang at 10:40 AM, fly back from Yichang at 12:00 PM, and arrive at the Hankou station at 2:25 PM in the afternoon. The entire route has three stops: (1) Hankou, (2) Shashi, (3) Yichang. Ticket prices are as follows: one-way: Hankou-Shashi 58 yuan, Hankou-Yichang 87 yuan, Shashi-Yichang 29 yuan; round-trip: Hankou-Shashi 98 yuan, Hankou-Yichang 148 yuan, Shashi-Yichang 50 yuan. The free baggage allowance is 20 pounds, and the excess weight fee is one yuan per pound for Hankou-Shashi and 5 jiao per pound for Shashi-Yichang. For airmail between Shanghai and Yichang, an airmail stamp of 3 jiao must be affixed.

Ham Industry Strenuously Contests Business Tax 165

▲Favorable Results from Petitioning in Beijing

The Shanghai Ham Industry Association previously sent representatives to Beijing to petition for a reduction in the ham business tax. Ham merchants from various places also sent representatives to Beijing at the same time. Within a few days, a total of 24 representatives from eight places, including Jinhua, Hangzhou, Suzhou, Zhenjiang, Yangzhou, Jiaxing, Nanjing, and Shanghai, arrived. They organized the Jiangzhe Provinces Ham Industry Representatives Petition Delegation in Beijing and began petitioning the day before yesterday (the 5th). They first went to the Ministry of Finance, where Section Chief Zhou Gangren of the Tax Division came out to meet them. Cai Xiaohe, Qi Wenwei, Xu Ruiqing, and Yu Weiqing were elected from among the representatives to speak and present their grievances. The outcome of the talks was very satisfactory. According to the Ministry of Finance, it is also aware that ham is indeed a farmer's byproduct. Although Jiangsu and Zhejiang have stipulated 15 per mille, the Ministry of Finance also knows that it should be reduced. However, the extent of the reduction has been discussed at five meetings and has not yet been determined. In any case, it will not be contrary to people's livelihood. The Ministry will convey the intention of the representatives to the minister. The delegation then went to the Ministry of Industry, where Minister Kong personally met them and promised to forward the request to the Ministry of Finance for review and reduction, and encouraged the ham merchants to improve the quality of ham materials in order to develop exports. The representatives were very satisfied with Minister Kong's instructions. After leaving, they went to the Central Party Headquarters and the Executive Yuan of the National Government to petition, and were all very satisfied.

Machinery Association Telegraphs Request to Correct Cumbersome Inspections 168

▲Telegram to the Ministry of Finance

The Shanghai Machinery Association telegraphed the Ministry of Finance regarding the obstruction of transportation of cotton textiles, saying: "To the esteemed Ministry of Finance of the National Government: The collection of the cotton yarn unified tax

on goods that have already been woven from cotton yarn, such as towels, socks, cloth, blankets, undershirts, and sanitary flannel shirts, etc., is not to be taxed again. This was originally the government's intention to reorganize the new tax system and eliminate the old and bad tax rules, in order to comply with the principle of one tax per item. The intention is good, and the implementation is also free from drawbacks. However, since the implementation of the new tax, there have been regulations on separate transportation. For example, the same goods that have already been taxed are transported separately from Place A to Places B and C. Place A has already been taxed, but Places B and C are again detained and the tax certificates are inspected. There are also regulations on transshipment. For example, goods that have already been taxed in Place A are transported to Place B and then transshipped to Place C in batches, and the tax certificates must be inspected repeatedly. The procedures are cumbersome and unhelpful, and only cause confusion. As a result, customs brokers have been incited to stop loading and transporting, and the reporting and transportation of woven products have been withdrawn, resulting in obstruction of commercial transportation and the stagnation of commercial goods. It is believed that the state's implementation of new taxes is originally intended to promote benefits and eliminate malpractices. The simpler and more convenient the handling procedures, the more conducive to promotion. Therefore, the collecting agencies should strictly inspect at the port of import and when leaving the factory to prevent untaxed cotton yarn textiles from being smuggled out. This method eliminates the need for cumbersome and repetitive tax certificate inspections, which cause hardship to merchants and the public, and will certainly not affect the state's tax revenue. Is this appropriate? It is requested that the Ministry investigate and quickly instruct the Customs and Unified Tax Bureaus to correct the cumbersome inspection procedures for transshipment and separate transportation in order to alleviate the suffering of the people. This is extremely urgent. [Signed] Shanghai National Goods Machinery Factories Association."

Trade Associations of Various Industries Must Not Convene Representative Assemblies on Their Own 170

▲City Executive Committee Orders City Chamber of Commerce to Rectify

The Shanghai Special Municipality Party Executive Committee issued an order to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating: "For the matter of ordering rectification: Trade associations of various industries are originally members of the Chamber of Commerce, and the Chamber of Commerce is the legal entity formed by the collective organization of various trade associations. If there are important commercial incidents or special issues related to all industries that need to be discussed, the trade associations of various industries should request the Chamber of Commerce Executive Committee to discuss them in accordance with the law. If it is deemed extremely important and it is considered necessary to convene a meeting of member representatives, it can also be requested in accordance with the law. There is no need for various industries to convene representative assemblies of trade associations on their own, which would only create discord. However, on the 4th of this month, various newspapers in this city published news that the trade associations of various industries in this city convened a representative assembly of various trade associations at the Chamber of Commerce due to the Central Government's amendment to Article 10 of the Implementing Rules of the Trade Association Law. This kind of action is extremely inappropriate and should be rectified immediately. Furthermore, after investigation, the trade associations of various industries in this city have successively formed the Industry Regulations Maintenance Committee and the Business Tax Rules Research Committee, etc., which have no legal basis. If there is a need for organization or research, it can also be requested that the Chamber of Commerce handle it; otherwise, the duplication of efforts will inevitably lead to confusion and discord in the business community's opinions in the future. The Chamber of Commerce is the main body of commercial organizations in this city and is responsible for guiding the various trade associations. If any of the above-mentioned violations of laws and regulations are discovered, they must be rectified immediately. Therefore, this order instructs the Chamber to comply with it. Strictly adhere to this order."

Strictly Prohibit Children from Performing Arts 176

The Chinese Children's Welfare Society, in view of the fact that there are often street performers in Shanghai who cruelly force children to perform arts in public and extort money, which violates humanity, sent letters to the police authorities of the Chinese and Foreign Concessions, requesting strict investigation and prohibition. After receiving a letter from Director Chen of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, a circular was issued yesterday to various district offices, stating: "According to a letter from the Chinese Children's Welfare Society, there are street performers in the concession who use cruel methods to treat the children they use, such as having a child bend over and grab their feet with their hands, forming a circle, and the street performer then uses a wooden stick to string them up, with two people carrying them or one person standing on their abdomen, soliciting money from the audience. Such a situation is inhumane. In addition, there are acts such as climbing a mountain of knives, going through a circle of knives, and hiding in a wine jar, all kinds of suffering, which are greatly harmful to the physical condition of young children. If we do not request prohibition, it would violate humanity. The duties of this Bureau are related, and we cannot remain silent. In addition to distribution, this order instructs everyone to pay attention. If you encounter such street performers, strictly prohibit them to emphasize humanity."

Real Estate Association Re-admonishes Water Company 177

▲Wording of British Consulate's Reply

The Shanghai Real Estate Association sent a letter to the British Shanghai Waterworks Company yesterday, stating: "Dear Sirs, we have received your reply of February 13 and are aware of its contents. In our letter of the 6th, we mentioned that your company's coercive actions are offensive and violate your country's policy of friendship with China. Your failure to refute these points indicates that you acknowledge them as undeniable facts. However, your company still insists on continuing to be wrong about the additional water fee, showing that you are unwilling to think reasonably. We are very disappointed. What we hope for is not ill-gotten wealth. Your company should not take what it should not from others, and real estate owners should not give what they should not to others. However, your company clearly knows that charging an additional water fee is an inappropriate act, but in order to maintain its continued acquisition of improper profits, it uses the excuse of custom, 4% for foreign residences, 5% for Chinese residences, and otherwise increasing the price rate. This is even more inappropriate. We believe that bad customs should be corrected immediately. Landlords collect rent and water fees on behalf of the water company, and including the water fee in the gross rent was originally for convenience of collection. If the water fee is collected directly by your company, the landlords will naturally remove the water fee. However, your company uses this simple procedure to create the bad custom of charging an additional water fee. We recall that seven years ago, your company repeatedly changed its regulations and applied them retroactively, causing landlords to have to pay tips for as long as three years. This has also become a custom. You do your best to comply with customs that benefit your company, but customs that are not beneficial to your company, you even break the law and do not apply the principle of non-retroactivity, and do not hesitate to cite the old events of 6% for Chinese residences and 5% for foreign residences. This has no relationship to the issue of charging an additional water fee, but it is enough to prove your company's past shame of unfair treatment of Chinese and foreign residences. You also said that if the rent is calculated according to the actual rent, the price rate will inevitably increase. We believe that it should increase in fact, and if it is legal and reasonable, we should accept it. However, we are unwilling to have a low name but a high reality, and we are especially unwilling to see people being forced to hand over a kind of money that they have no obligation to pay by law or reason, and being seized by violent and coercive means without claiming restitution according to law, or even continuing to pay. Your company said that the current price rate will end this year and be considered again next year. However, we are extremely unwilling to see your company continue to use violent and coercive means in these few months, intending to or actually seizing improper profits. Accordingly, we re-admonish you and hope that you will jointly abide by the law."

Also, the association previously sent a letter to British Consul-General Sir Brenan regarding the water issue, requesting him to stop it according to law. The association received a reply from Consul Brenan yesterday, stating: "(Above omitted) (A letter dated February 28 regarding the dispute between the Shanghai Waterworks Company and Xingping Company over the payment of water prices). According to my investigation, the clause in the contract stating 'actual rent paid without reduction' is interpreted as gross rent not only by the Waterworks Company but also by the Public Works Department. This interpretation has been in effect for more than forty years and is not without reason. It has also been tacitly approved by custom and the times. Your association's opposition seems to lack a strong basis, and I am not in a position to interfere directly. I am sorry to disappoint you. Respectfully submitted, etc."

Robbery and Killing of Victim at Baxianqiao 179

▲Two Robbers Enter the House

▲"Please Help, Boss"

▲Shop Owner Shouts "Robbers!"

▲Three Shots in Succession Cause Death

At around 8 o'clock yesterday morning, a robbery occurred at the Mao surname iron car clothing store located at No. 53, Maigao Baolu Road, Baxianqiao, in the French Concession. The robbers opened fire and killed the shop owner on the spot. The details are as follows:

The shop owner has a violent nature. The owner of Mao Anji Iron Car Clothing Store (north of Baxianqiao Xiaocai Market) at No. 53, Lane Entrance, Fifth Lane, Shou'anli, Maigao Baolu Road, French Concession, is Ningbo native Mao Anhong, who is 43 years old this year. The store has been open for 18 years, but Mao has a violent nature. His wife, Tong, died ten years ago due to miscarriage and typhoid fever. Mao refused to treat her, and Tong hated him and swallowed the gold ring she wore on her ear and committed suicide, leaving behind two daughters and one son. The eldest daughter, Amao, is 18 years old this year, the son, Jinquan, is 15 years old this year, and the youngest daughter, Xiaomao, is 11 years old this year.

▲Expelled Mother-in-law and Children At that time, after Mao's wife died, the children were young and no one to take care of them, so his mother-in-law, Tong Shi, came to the store to help take care of the children. Three years ago, Mao had an affair with a woman surnamed Wu, also from his hometown, who is 31 years old this year, and brought her to live in the store. Mao increasingly abused his children, and his mother-in-law often argued with him. The year before last, Mao expelled his mother-in-law and children together and moved them to No. 4, Chonganli, Lafeide Road.

The robbers visited early in the morning. His concubine Wu gave birth to a girl last month. Mao is very fond of Wu. At nearly 8 o'clock yesterday morning, the store door had just opened, and apprentice Ma Gen (18 years old) was working at the counter. Mao had not yet gotten up. Wu got up, emptied the chamber pot, and returned to the room. While sitting on the chamber pot urinating, two robbers dressed in long gowns and speaking in Ningbo dialect suddenly came into the store and pushed the apprentice into Mao's bedroom (in the back of the store), forbidding him to make a sound. The robbers then said, "Please help, boss."

▲The victim was killed on the spot. After saying that, one robber immediately acted, first taking off a gold bracelet and a gold ring from Wu's hand (the bracelet weighed about five qian and the ring weighed about three qian), and a gold ring from Mao's hand (weighing about two qian), and wanted to escape with the loot. At that time, Mao was still lying in bed and shouted "Robbers!" The robbers immediately turned back and fired a gun at Mao, and two shots rang out. The bullets hit Mao's right rib cage and penetrated his thigh. Mao still got up with injuries, intending to pursue them. The robbers fled to the door of the store and turned back and fired another shot, hitting Mao in the throat, and he immediately fell to the ground and died.

▲Both Robbers Fled. The robbers immediately fled outwards, escaping northwards from Hongyunfang Lane behind the Nanjing Grand Theater towards the west and disappeared without a trace. Later, the Songshan Road Police Station in charge of the area was informed and immediately ordered detectives to investigate. At the same time, Mao's body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuantang autopsy office. Zhu, the judge of the French Court, was reported by the criminal section of the General Patrol Station and arrived at the office at noon to verify the body. He sat in the public seat after clarifying the body, and the detective reported the details of the case first.

▲The Main Wife Narrated the Case. According to the description of his wife Wu, her husband was shot and killed by robbers. Judge Zhu instructed that the body of Mao Anhong, who had died, was indeed shot and killed by robbers while he was alive. After taking pictures, the wife was allowed to prepare a coffin and collect the body, and the police station was ordered to strictly arrest the robbers and bring them to justice. According to the wife, one robber was wearing a woolen camel hair robe and a flower satin mandarin jacket, with a melon-skin small hat with a red knot on his head, who was the one who fired the gun, and the clothes of the robber who committed the robbery were not clearly seen. Now the family of the deceased is allowed to collect the body this morning.

Public Bus Crashes into Reception Room 180

▲To Avoid a Bicycle...Caused the Accident

▲Unable to Enter the Door...Breaks Through the Wall

▲Western Woman Sitting in the Bus...Injured

At around 2 pm yesterday, a No. 15058, Route 9 public bus traveling between Yangshupu and Daxilu Road, when passing the intersection of Fuxu Road and Hadong Road, turned the rudder to the side to give way to a bicycle, but it was too late to brake, and drove onto the sidewalk. Because the wheels were out of control, it continued to move forward after going up the stairs, causing the front of the bus to crash into the reception room of the Tang family at No. 602. Fortunately, except for an old woman in the room, there were no others, and the place where the old woman was sitting was far away from the window and did not meet the front of the bus, so she was not harmed. At that time, the public bus was traveling from east to west, and the bicycle seemed to come out of Hadong Road and wanted to turn into Fuxu Road to the west, which caused the public bus to give way and caused this disaster. No. 602 is a three-story house at the bottom of Minhoulida Street near the street. When the No. 15058 public bus crashed into the wall, its position was very close to the door. Although the driver was anxious to brake, it was too late, causing the front of the bus to drill straight into the window. However, the window was too small to accommodate this behemoth, so the walls around it loosened and fell, until a huge hole appeared in the wall, and the front of the bus fell into the house. Except for a western woman, the passengers on the bus were fortunately unharmed. The western woman, named Lv Fuqiti, seemed to be of Russian origin, and was sent to Hongen Hospital on Daxilu Road for treatment. It was generally fine, but the tables, chairs, magnetic bottles and decorations in the reception room of No. 602 had all become powder.
